Very cool.	LIFE BIRD #536!  Heard a call that I thought might be a call of a wild foul, and I immediately hoped Chukar.  I listened to my recording of one, and indeed it was.  How unsatisfying it would be to just hear one and not see it.  I began scanning the area to the south on the hillside outside the fenced in area.  BINGO...game bird, bright red beak, two birds, right markings.  I was so excited, I carefully noted the location of the birds and walked around the board walk and hiked out of the fenced in area and up the hillside to the location where I saw the birds sure that there was no way they would get away from me finding them again.  WRONG!  So though it wasn't a completely satisfying sighting, and in my excitement I failed to take a photo from where I first found them with my glasses, I did get a detailed and good look at the two birds for about 2 minutes, plus I heard one bird call once, and saw it call a second time.

The site is ~2 miles E of County Road 3 up a Cyn in the Butte Mountains for which there was the vaguest of tracks to drive. Near my camp the Cyn bottom is grassy with sparse Artemisia and saltbush. Higher up the Cyn floor has more Pinyon and Juniper. I surmise that the area was heavily impacted by miners whenever that was. 100+ years ago?  Rock formations were chipped and rubble remains below. My hike up the canyon ended at 39.72735. -115.30565, which is 1.6 km straight line from my start point (my camp). So I hiked at least 3.2km round trip.  End point elev is between 6919' and 6869'.  Peregrine eyrie on the south cyn wall with, I think, a sub-ad bird tending. I was surprised to not see any Parids here.
